Annex C
SOCIO-CULTURAL



Cl SOCIO-CULTURAL STUDY



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                   IL),-;,         v   S\
1      INTRODUCTION
This Socio Cultural Study was conducted to cover the sociological aspects of SES
city, in line with the broader study on "EIA for SES Airport, aimed to provide the
background for the construction of the new terminal. As such, this rpnnrt rnvprc
the social dimensions of the community, in relation to the expected extension of
the Airport. The approach here is to provide a description of the social
environment, with the objective of providing as clear as possible a picture of the
society of SES, as well as the views of the target population vis-a-vis the new
terminal. The target population here Is diversified, including the inhabitants of
the city, both native and migrant, in addition to the tourists.
The rationale for the social study is to Investigate the impact of the extension on
the community, as perceived through the eyes of the above-mentioned target
population. The underlying factor is that the construction of the new terminal has
an expected positive impact on SES, not only on the area of tourism, but
extends to include the overall socio-economic conditions of the city. By creating
job opportunities, increasing the services, and expectedly resulting in more pull
factors in the community, the situation will eventually lead to a more booming
socio-economic life.
This Study, in its attempt to achieve the above-mentioned objective, presents
the data from the different sources, in line with the terms of reference, followed
by a field study covering the target population, as will be described in detail in
the methodology. Here results and analysis will be presented, leading to
proposed recommendations, as stemming from the above-given data.
Methodoloav
The Study includes two (2) sections:
The first section describes the social environment, as has been collected from
different sources, most of which are official. These sources are:
-   The Information Sector from the SES City Council
-   The Central Agency for Public Mobilization and Statistics (CAPMAS)
-   The Gulf of Aqaba Environmental Action Plan (GAEAP)
-   The Statistical Guide of SES City
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)           Page 3 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                &J       .        ,     .r
-   The reports from the Authority for Urban Planning.
It is important to mention that there is an obvious variation in the data collected
from the different sources. Moreover, data have not been updated.
Consequently, the study has concentrated on the most recent daiL avaiiau.ie
though mostly are not up to the current year.
The second section of the report covers the results and analysis of the field
study. The methodology adopted is as follows:
Sarmnlina
It was decided to use a purposeful sample, based on criteria of selection for the
target population. These are:
-   Government and Airport employees
-   Hotel employees
-   Tourists
-   Shop/bazaar owners
The Government and hotel employees were selected because of their indirect
involvement with the Airport, whereas the employees on the premises have a
more direct involvement. Shop/bazaar owners are directly affected by the
coming tourists. The tourists them selves are the main targets of the project.
SamRlina Criteria
Selection was made to Include different levels of the employees; namely: top
level executives, middle range, and lower level. As for the hotels, both managers
and employees of middle ranks were interviewed. The idea was to make sure
that responses cover different categories in order to insure diversification of
responses, representing the perception of the respective levels. Shop/bazaar
owners were selected from those already doing business In the existing terminal,
those associated with hotels, and independent ones, also to cover different
locations, and as such representing different angles of perception.
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)            Page 4 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                               &   ,- /Ji!)
The age group of the employees ranges between the thirties and sixties,
representing the median for the productive segment in the community-in other
words, those in the active labor market, whose views are relevant to the
research objective.
Tourist selection covered different countries of origin. They are from Belgium,
England, Germany, Kuwait, the United Arab Emirates, and Egypt. Naturally, no
age specification was considered.
Research Method
It was decided to use an In-depth, open-ended approach for the field study. A
guide interview schedule was designed for each of the four (4) groups, whereby
the researcher could probe during the interview. Selection of this method has the
advantage of allowing a deep insight into the issues under study, rather than
providing a superficial response in this respect. Since the points under
investigation need a good understanding of the situatlon, the open-ended
questions are here preferred.
In addition, a quick public opinion poll was used to help get the feel of the
average person as to the construction of the new terminal.
Copies of the interview guide schedules as well as the public opinion questions
are attached in this Annex.
Sample Size
The qualitative approach, as here used, depends on a small number of
respondents, since the interviews include an in-depth, probing subject matter
that necessitates an equally In-depth, probing analysis. As such, the sample size
here is one hundred and twenty (120) respondents, constituting thirty (30)
individuals from each respective group.
Allowance was made to diversify the ranks in each group, as has already been
mentioned.
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)           Page S of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                &       i&,-j    J9r\t
The quick public opinion poll was conducted on twenty-five (25) individuals,
selected on a random basis, with no particular specifications to age, gender, or
education. The sample here was not meant to represent specific categories,
since as above mentioned, the objective of this poll was to help and give a feel
of the average person, and as a complementary method.
The findings of the field investigations are presented in item 3.
2      DEMOGRAPHIC AND SOCIAL CHARACTERISTICS
This part represents the demographic and social characteristics as related to the
followings:
Population
Since the restoration of SES to Egypt in 1982, the City has been developing and
growing in response to the rising demand of not only the influx of tourists from
all parts of the world, but also that of the inhabitants whose numbers are
increasing over the years. This Section addresses the following issues as related
to population:
Size and Urban/Rural Distribution
Table (C- 1) and Figure (C- 1) show the population increase between the years
1986 and 2002, distributed between rural and urban areas.

Projected Increase in the Population
Projections for the City based on the current trend indicate a growing population
of 9.6% annually (Plan for SES City in 2017). It is, therefore, expected that in
the year 2017 the population will reach 85,000 inhabitants.
The Gulf of Aqaba Environmental Plan Action projects the increase in the
population in SES as growing from 22,000 in 1997 to 48,000 in 2002, to 70,000
in 2017, based on the dramatic expansion, " to meet the demand for workers
generated by the tourism industry".
Table (C- 4) and Figure (C- 4 shows the expected change in demographic
characteristics, as implemented by the Authority of Urban Development in its
proposed plans for the City until the year 2017.

labor.
-   Family size, for the same reason, Is expected to increase.
-   The number of children below fifteen (15) years will eventually rise.
-   The elderly segment, 60+, Is likewise expected to increase, as the existing
younger segment will reach this age.

indicators in the education process a point that is highly encouraged. The fact
remains that with the expected increase in the population the question is raised
on how far this reasonable student/teacher ratio can be maintained.
There are, also, private schools in the city, comprising one English, utie rireimil,
and one German. These are totally independent of the Egyptian administration.
As expensive as they are in terms of tuition, they cater to the rich people in the
community, mostly those in the hotel business, including the expatriates for the
most part. (Information Center in SES).
Health
There are three (3) hospitals in the city, estimated as one hospital for every
3609 persons. Their current capacities are 177 beds. There are 66 doctors and
54 nurses. The Central Hospital is responsible for primary health care, as seen in
vaccination and maternal and child health care. Government employees have
medical insurance. Each hotel provides the same for its employees. There are
also some private clinics.
Non-aovernmental Organizations (NGO's)
The City has three (3) NGO's, namely;
-   The Society for Investors: In addition to their involvement with investment/
business, the members are concerned about the welfare of the City and are
involved in upgrading projects, especially the one related to the
environment.
-   The Diving Society: It is concerned with divers and their activities.
-   The Society for Community Development:    This society is under the
administration of the Ministry of Social Affairs. It provides aid to the needy,
especially from among the bedouins. This segment of the population
constitutes its major target beneficiaries. It also works in community
development in the form of providing literacy classes and developing health
awareness programs.
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)            Page 14 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                  ,          b        it9r\B
Recreational Activities
The spread-out of hotels and resorts do not cater to the residents who constitute
the working force. Consequently, the municipality has provided public beaches
and parks, free of charge to be within their financial means for tneir use.
Caterers are granted the license to serve refreshments and food in these places
on an optional basis, and with no obligation on the part of the public.
Residents of the City believe that they benefit from this procedure, because the
caterers are concerned about environmental matters and therefore, physical
conditions are properly maintained.
Housing
Hotels and resorts serve the tourists. The residents who are employed in the
City, however, are given housing facilities. The Government employees are
provided with relatively low- cost housing, except for the upper echelons that get
higher levels of housing. Hotels are also responsible for providing housing for
their employees.
It is interesting to note that taxi drivers reported that they couldn't afford
housing, so they sleep in the taxis. Drivers spend around three (3) weeks in the
City and go back to their families for the remaining period of the month. During
their absence, a partner takes over the responsibility of the taxi.
4      TOURISM
Tourism is one of the fastest growing industries in Egypt, a primary source of
foreign exchange earnings, US$ 3.8 billion in Financial Year 2002/2003 and an
appreciable contribution towards the country's balance of payments. As a labor-
intensive service industry in a country struggling with underemployment,
tourism is of paramount Importance in Egypt's present and future economic
development.
The project area, in particular, is based primarily on tourism. The sun, sand,
mountains, clean air, wildlife, abundant coral reefs and religious and cultural
sites constitute its competitive advantage and primary attraction for international
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)           Page 15 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP
and domestic tourists, and contribute to Egypt's reputation as a world class
tourism destination.
The project area current number of hotel rooms Is 26036, 19% of the total
number of hotel rooms in Egypt, and is projected to provide 450u-u iuuilb uy
2017 for an assumed maximum of 81000 guests.
The number of hotels in the city is shown in Table (C- 7)

is a point worthy of consideration in planning for the provision of services
required for the target beneficiaries.
It is important to mention in this respect that the bedouins, who are the native
population of the region, participate in touristic activities, in agreement with the
hotel management. Bedouins provide what are known as "bedouln nights",
where they exhibit their folk culture for purposes of entertainment to the
tourists. Music, dancing, and even food of the native culture are part and parcel
of the activity, with a bedouin atmosphere surrounding the site, which is usually
a tent of the local style.

quality of the water. In addition, the area suffers from insects, especially
mosquitoes and an insect that appears in winter, known as "sand fly".
The prospects of the new terminal as seen by this group of interviewees tend to
concentrate on the positive side. The City will flourish and the buwiit:bb vvmi
boom. This situation will result from the increase in the influx of tourists.
However, in this case there will arise the need to provide more services
consequently more employees will be attracted to the City in response to the
rising demand in this respect.
Only one respondent believes that the terminal will raise the number of Incoming
tourists, and the environment will be affected negatively, as there will be more
pressure on marine life and land resources. This respondent is a middle-range
employee in the City municipality. Government employees are satisfied with
their life in the city as being quiet and relaxed.
Hotel Employees
People In this category come from different Governorates. Housing is provided
by the hotels. However, no complaints appeared among this group. Most of the
respondents live single, even the married ones. Because housing is communal,
they need special permission to bring their wives along, but on a temporary
basis. Housing for families is provided for employees at the level of
management.
Five (5) respondents among this group feel that the new terminal is necessary,
because the current situation in the Airport cannot accommodate the increasing
number of tourists.
Prospects for the new terminal also indicate a positive outlook among these
respondents. They emphasize, however, the need to Increase services in the
City, including more road construction in response to the rising demand of
tourism.
There appeared a certain worry among hotel employees, which they share with
the above-mentioned government employee, when they emphasize the negative
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)          Page 20 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                d,i4LZJ è 
impact of the influx of tourists on the environment-namely, coral reefs, marine
life, and the mountain terrain.
Hotel occupancy is subject to seasonal changes, as well as variation In the type
of guests. Winter has the most attraction for Westerners, while Egyptians appear
more during school holidays.
It Is Interesting to note that noise does not represent a problem among either
groups. Only in Hotel Gardenia was the problem of noise mentioned bv the
employees. The hotel lies close to the Airport. This proximity has created a
problem of noise that the tourists complain about, as reported by the hotel
personnel. The question remains as to what the situation will be like after the
construction of the new terminal.
Interestingly enough, though the personnel In Gardenia Hotel expressed their
worry about noise in relation to guests, they did not see the same situation as a
problem to them. Their housing is likewise close to the Airport, and subjected to
the same pollution. However, this does not constitute a source of worry to them.
Other hotels in the same proximity have partially handled this problem with
implementing some mitigation measures to minimize the effect of noise such as
the installing of double glazed windows, as is the case with Hotel Savoy and
Coral Beach El Montaza.
Business Owners and Employees
The Interviewees here were selected from among those having their business in
the Airport zone, in hotels, and independent activities.
The four (4) shops in the Airport zone are engaged in the sale of all sorts of
touristic goods, namely; gold, silver, leather, papyrus, and different souvenirs.
The shops are rented for 1075 L.E. per square meter per month. Owners are
willing to have shops in the new terminal. They are ready to pay a higher rent,
though reluctantly, but prefer to function on the basis of monopoly for each
respective activity. is are 2000 L.E. per square meter.
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)            Page 21 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                                       j., p \
These shops are currently located in an open space, where each shop takes a
corner to exhibit its goods. Owners here are not happy about this situation, and
express explicitly that the new terminal should have clearly defined and
designated areas for each respective shop. In this way, business can proceed in
a more organized fashion.
Their business is subject to seasonal changes the high seasons normally are In
December, March and April. The summer months represent the low season,
except this year  (2003).  The high seasons are dominated by expatriate
tourists, mostly from the West. Egyptians come to the City during school
holidays, in particular in the mid-year holiday.
In Neama Bay, the shops are mostly owned by bedouins and rented to those
who run them. There are also shops rented from hotels. Most of those involved
in the business are migrants to the City, also from different Governorates. Goods
are mostly delivered through land routes.
The length of the period of the establishment varies between three (3) and
fifteen (15) years.
Interviewees believe that the new terminal is good for business. Three among
them see that the current situation in the airport is bad and that the service is
bad. They believe that the new terminal will solve the problems of crowd.
Interviewees from this group have no worries about environmental problems. An
interesting statement was made by one of them, "We can tolerate the noise from
airplanes if it means better business for us. Noise in this case is a simple price
to pay.'
Tourists
Tourists interviewed were from different countries, namely; Belgium, England,
Germany, Kuwait, the United Arab Emirates, and Egypt.
Interestingly enough, all respondents without exception are satisfied with the
current situation in the Airport, in terms of service, treatment by personnel, and
general condition. One tourist from Belgium said, 'If people complain about
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)            Page 22 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP
overcrowding here, look what the situation is like in the Airport In Belgium.
There is more overcrowding there." This Belgian, however, criticized the dirty
streets around the Airport, a complaint that was repeated by almost all
respondents from this group.
Complaints were more common among Egyptian tourists. One woman expressed
her disapproval of overcrowding; another complained about the dirty Airport; a
man considered the cafeteria in a very poor condition; a fourth person believed
that the number of employees in the Airport is not enough to provide the needed
service. Still another Egyptian complained that the Airport personnel treat the
foreigners better than the Egyptians; while another criticized the way the bazaar
personnel treat the tourists in general.
The visit to SES Is not the first for all respondents except one from Kuwait. He
said that this is his first visit, because he has heard a lot about the City.
Interviewees from among the tourists do not have any objection to the new
terminal. They come, anyway, but the new terminal will definitely attract more
tourists, in their point of view.
Opinion Poll
Unanimously, the answers support the construction of the new terminal, as a
"necessary", "civilized project", and " a civilized front" for SES. Two (2)
respondents went as far as saying that there is an urgent need for it. In this
way, tourism will definitely flourish and the Egyptian economy will consequently
benefit. One (1) respondent asserted that the new terminal can help solve any
possible existing problems in the terminal and it is hoped that the Airport
services will be upgraded.
It follows that the impact as seen by this group is on the positive side. It will
enhance Egypt's reputation/image as a country of -tourism. However, it is
interesting to know that ten (10) individuals emphasized the need to study
properly this impact in terms of solid waste, heights of buildings, marine life, and
existing buildings. It must be mentioned that the group of respondents here are
individuals apparently with a reasonably high level of education.
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)            Page 23 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP
Involuntary Resettlement
The project area does not include any resettlement/relocation of the population.
As such, it does not raise problems related to the displacement of inhabitants in
any form. The Bedouins, who represent the native population in SES, ivc i,, Li;.
valleys and are not, therefore, subjected to these procedures. Although they
retain their own cultural life style, they are, nevertheless, integrated in the
economic activities of the SES community, as here mentioned.
Moreover, the land allocated for the Airport extension is a public area, falling
under governmental administration. The land owner ship is transferred to EAC
through the Presidential decree / 2003. Currently, the land is not used for any
economical activity. The land acquisition form together with a copy of the
Presidential Decree is available in the attachments.
It follows, therefore, that the construction of the new building will not cause any
involuntary resettlement issues. Hence, the World Bank Operational Policy OP/BP
4.12 will not be triggered.
It is the intention of the EHCAAN and EAC to handle the operation of the new
terminal to a management company. The EHCAAN indicates that discussions will
be undertaken with the managing company to guarantee that employees in the
airport fall under the jurisdiction of the Egyptian Labor Laws, which specify
clearly against lay-offs of employed personnel. In the case of the new terminal,
therefore, there is no threat of lay-offs for the currently employed personnel.
7      CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
In line with the above presentation of the current situation in SES, coupled with
the results and analysis of the field study, a number of recommendations can be
cited, relevant to the existing and projected social conditions:
-   Since the construction of the new terminal is considered both a need and
necessity as the City is developing, the implementation of the project will
eventually create more job opportunities, not only in the Airport, but also in
the City itself. It is estimated that more jobs will be created, according to
the proposed employment plan. This situation will necessarily raise the
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)           Page 24 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                     ,J                           i     ,-A
demand for more services at different levels. It becomes essential,
therefore, for the Airport Authority to guarantee the provision of these
services for its personnel. One can argue that this is the municipality's
responsibility. The fact remains that if the booming of the City requires
added efforts on the part of the Municipallty, this task falls unaer mne
responsibility of the Authority where its employees are concerned.
Major In the provision of services Is the guarantee for the good quality of
housing, more emphasis should be given, since current complaints of the
employees at the Government and Airport levels Is related to the Door
quality of both environmental and residential conditions.
Shops/bazaars are in demand In the Airport zone. A proper environment for
their business needs to be established in order to allow for the proper
procedure of matters, since the current situation within the area of open
space in the existing terminal Is not only visually unacceptable, but more so,
creates an environment which lacks organization/structure. Shops/bazaars
with clear boundaries are, therefore, needed.
Although most of the tourists expressed approval of the current situation In
the Airport, it may be necessary to have an orientation program for the
employees, whereby they are given special instructions as to how to treat
the tourists. A major component of this program should be the equally good,
polite treatment of tourists, both foreigners and Egyptians alike.
Needless to say, maintaining a clean environment inside and outside the
Airport is top priority. In this case, it may be necessary to increase the
number of employees responsible for this task.
It is important to mention that the plan for the City should consider the
increase In the population size as well as in the number of the incoming
tourists whether the terminal Is constructed or not. It follows, therefore,
that its construction will help alleviate the pressure on the existing Airport.
It becomes necessary, therefore, to build the new terminal taking into
consideration the above points in order to guarantee positive results and
avoid any earlier mistakes.
The hotels/resorts in the Nabq region are located in proximity to the take off
side of the terminal. Some of these hotels have already been built in area
declared as no-construction zone. This situation raises questions that need
to be handled in line with regulations as well as practicalities, because
already complaints from some resorts have been legally filed e.g., as is the
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)             Page 25 of 34
Annex C - Social Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP
case of Hauza resort, lying at the take off side and being exposed to a
significantly high level of noise.
-   The exposure of the Airport personnel to environmental hazards, especially
those working in solid waste disposal, necessitates good medical service
whereby they are subjected to regular check-ups. It is-understouu Eildd Ethey
are provided with a health insurance system. The recommendation here,
however, Is to guarantee their health safety with regular check ups.
-   With the intention of awarding the operation of the Airport to a management
company, the division of roles should be clearly identified. All mitiaation
measures that may be needed to mitigate potential social and economical
adverse impacts of such agreement should be identified and implemented.
All necessary measures tat may be needed to reserve worker rights in the
light of the applicable local laws.

ANNEX E
*        ECONOMICAL STUDY



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                               j  6tW.sr\U
ECONOMIC IMPACT ANALYSIS
FOR
THE NEW EXTENSION OF SES AIRPORT
1.    OBJECTIVE AND SCOPE OF WORK
Having recognized that tourism is a major potential source of revenue and foreign
exchange to Egypt in general and to the Red Sea area in particular, the Government
of Egypt with the full support of the World Bank Is now embarking upon an extension
of SES Airport in order to meet the increasing number of tourists, which would result
in large and increasing traffics in the Airport area. The viability of the extension of
SES Airport from the society's point of view would depend on both the financial and
economic returns on such an investment.
The objective of this analysis is to test the economic viability of the proposed
extension of SES Airport. It is evaluated on the basis of five economic parameters;
Economic Returns, Value Added, Employment, Foreign Exchange Earnings and Tax
Revenue, in an attempt to appraise the soundness and acceptability of the underlying
extension from the standpoint of the society, i.e. national profitability.
Financial analysis Included In the conducted feasibility study of the new extension of
the Airport is the first step in the economic evaluation of Social Capital Projects such
as Airports in that it is essential to test the commercial profitability of the project, in
order to attract capital investment. However, commercial profitability (financial
analysis) may not give a good idea of the contribution of a project to the national
economy. For measuring a project's contributiqn to the national economy, national
profitability (economic analysis) should be tested.
Commercial profitability and national profitability differ in many ways. The objective
of commercial profitability analysis is to assess the net financial results of a project,
while national profitability analysis traces the project's contribution to all fundamental
development objectives. Commercial profitability analysis is based on market prices
while national profitability Is determined with the help of adjusted prices, which are
deemed to be an approximation of true economic prices. For commercial profitability,
the time value of money is tackled by application of the private discount rate based
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)          Page 2 of 14
Annex E - Economy Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                 &4>-4)      ,        9
on the prevailing interest rate of the capital market, while In the case of national
profitability, it is solved by using the social discount rate.
These different concepts of profitability are reflected in the different items considered to
be costs and benefits and in their valuations. The two types of costs and benefits do not
coincide. A transfer of the control over resource allocation from one member or section of
society, to another does not represent direct claims on the country's resource. Also,
indirect benefits resulting from the project are not taken into account in the benefit
streams of the financial analysis. The flow of economic benefits and costs may be larger
or smaller than financial ones. This econornic impact analysis is concemed with the
contribution of the new extension of SES Airport to the national economy, in order to
justify the investment decisions taken on behalf of the society.
2.    APPROACH AND METHODOLOGY
The methodology used in the economic analysis of the new extension of SES Airport
began with the conversion of financial statements of the feasibility study conducted
by the Ministry of Civil Aviation into economic statements In order to arrive at the
flow of net benefits and economic Impact of the project over time.
In this respect, the soundness and acceptability of the new extension of the Airport
from the society's point of view Is based on the comparison between the additional
benefits resulted from the underlying project and the additional cost incurred. In
other words, the economic evaluation is based on the additional passengers expected
to visit the area as a result of establishing the new extension. Expected financial
revenue and economic benefits per passenger are therefore identified and quantified
to be converted into streams of financial revenues and economic benefits respectively
on the basis of the expected additional passengers per annum to be weighted against
the additional investment cost and cost of operation. The derived net benefits are
measured on annual basis over the expected life of the new extension of the Airport.
All inputs and outputs are valued at their economic prices, in order to compensate for
any price distortion. However, since all economic activities comprising the underlying
project are valued at free market prices, we can safely assume that prices of Inputs
and outputs in this project are not significantly distorted. However, all foreign
components are converted into Egyptian pounds based on the current market
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)            Page 3 of 14
Annex E - Economy Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                &it;^A)      ,       7V&
exchange rate US $1 = LE 6.3, with 10% contingency. Both benefit and cost items as
well as foreign exchange rate and social discount rate are based on constant prices of
the base year.
All future values are discounted at the social opportunity cost of capital, which is
expressed as the Social Discount Rate (SDR). The interest rate on long term loans at
which Egypt can actually borrow capital from the relevant International market,
currently around six percent (6%), Is taken as an appropriate basis for estimation of
the social discount rate. The Interest rate must then be adjusted to take into account
the prevailing economic and political conditions of Egypt as a net capital borrower. We
have added a premium of 0.67 to the international interest rate, in order to derive
the Social Discount Rate. The estimated premium is, to a considerable extent, an
educated guess based on expectation. The general purpose of using a discount rate
higher than the International rate of interest is to count for economic and political
risk.
The Social Discount Rate has been estimated as follows:
SDR      = I (1+P)
= 6% (1.67) = 10%
Where
SDR      = Social Discount Rate
i        = Rate of interest on the relevant world capital market
P        = Premium of domestic projects
The soundness and acceptability of the project from the society's point of view are
based on the following criteria, in order to test the economic viability of such an
i nvestment.
* Economic Rate of Return (ERR)
The Economic Rate of Return (ERR) reflects the discount rate that reduces the
present value of the future stream of net benefits from a project to zero. The project
will be economically viable If ERR is greater than SDR (10%).
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)           Page 4 of 14
Annex E - Economy Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                 @P4'WA      V b &V "\
* Present Value of Net Benefits
The net benefits generated by the project over its expected life is discounted at the
social discount rate to arrive at a present value, which can be compared with the
present value of the investment cost to test the economic viability of the project.
Economic viability implies that present value exceeds investment cost, i.e. positive
net present value.
* Present Value of National Value Added (PNVA)
Value added is the basic criterion for the overall effect of a project on the economy.
Value added represents, in a most general way, the difference between the output
value and inputs purchased from other units. The use of national value added (NVA)
rather than domestic value added is advocated because it excludes repatriation
payments of profits, management fees and salaries. In this respect, PNVA measures
the contribution of the project to the national economy in two different ways:
- Absolute Efficiency Test (AET) Is used as a measure of the net present value of
national value added, in order to test the economic acceptability of the project to
Egypt. The national value added is projected over a specified period and then
discounted at the social discount rate to arrive at an absolute value to be
compared with the present value of capital invested.
- Relative Efficiency Test (RET) is used to test the efficiency of capital invested in
the project. RET takes into account the scarcity of capital. The test measures the
value added per unit of capital (i.e. the marginal product of capital).
* Employment Effect
Creation of productive employment opportunities is one of the primary development
objectives of Egypt. Hence, the underlying extension is evaluated based on Its ability
to generate employment. Both direct and indirect employment are considered. Direct
employment refers to the new employment opportunities created within the new
extension of the Airport, while indirect employment refers to job opportunities created
by businesses in the study area (such as hotels, restaurants and shops).
* Foreign Exchange Effect (FEE)
An essential part of the overall evaluation of the project is the assessment of the effects on
the foreign exchange position of the country. In countries like Egypt, shortage of foreign
exchange could be a key obstacle to economic growth. Therefore, the effect on the
balance of payments should be tested. The net foreign exchange flows from the project are
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)            Page 5 of 14
Annex E - Economy Study



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                                     JV&9
estimated and discounted at the social discount rate to arrive at their present value, used as
a single criterion for evaluation. The present value of the net flow of foreign exchange
over the whole economic life measures the project's net contribution to, or drain from, the
foreign exchange pool of the country over a specified period.
3.    BASIS OF ESTIMATES
The economic evaluation of the new extension of SES Airport is based on the financial
feasibility study conducted by the Ministry of Civil Aviation, Egyptian Airports
Company, taking into consideration the economic benefits in one side and cost of
environmental mitigation on the other side. The following are the basis on which
economic impact of the new extension of the Airport is tested and evaluated:
* All prices are based on constant prices of the base year. Foreign
currency component (US Dollars) are converted at the current market
rate of 1 US $ = LE 6.3.
* SES Airport extension is expected to operate in 2006/2007, with a
construction period of 3 years.
*  Additional number of passengers classified  into Foreigners and
Egyptians is based on the difference between the expected number of
passengers (as estimated by the Ministry of Civil Aviation) and the
ceiling capacity of the existing Airport as of 2005 (3.35 million
passengers) as shown in Table El.
* Annual financial revenue per passenger is based on the estimate (fees
adjusted at the current market exchange rate) made by the Ministry of
Civil Aviation (the financial feasibility study) as shown in Table E2.
* Additional number of tourists Is estimated at 50% of the number of
passengers, i.e. two-way ticket.
* Direct Economic Expenditure per tourist. It should be noted that the
new extension of the Airport would have both direct and indirect
economic input on the economy. The Indirect impact is usually
measured through the multiplier effect (implicit effect). It is estimated
at 2.64 (ECES study), i.e. total effects are more than the double of the
direct effect. However, our estimate of economic effect is confined to
the direct effect as minimum economic effects.
It is based on the following:
-  Expenditure per tourist per night

- Foreign US $ 108
-  Egyptian  LE 80
Source: Ministry of Tourism "Foreign Visitor Expenditure Survey",
1996.
- Duration of stay
- Foreign   6 nights
- Egyptian  4 nights
Source: Ministry of Tourism, Tourists Development Authority, July
2003.
- Average profit represents 30% (for foreigner) and 20% (for Egyptians) of the
amount spent by the tourist.
Source: Makary Consulting. Analysis of revenue and cost of hotels, and
restaurants in SES, 2002.
- It is assumed that 50% of the Egyptians will use alternative means of
transportation, basically cars, to reach SES If the Airport is not extended.
*  Net expenditure Is estimated on the basis of the direct economic expenditure
taking Into consideration the average profit norms of tourism in Egypt i.e. 30%
(for foreigners) and 20% (for Egyptians).
* The financial costs, i.e. both investment cost (fixed cost and pre-opening
expenses) and costs of operation are based on the assumptions of the financial
feasibility study conducted by the Ministry of Aviation, taking into consideration
the additional number of passengers estimated that the new extension will
accommodate. All foreign components are adjusted at the current market
exchange rate of 1 US $ = LE 6.3.
*  The economic costs, i.e. mitigation costs are based on the estimates conducted by the
experts, each in his field distributed on the lifetime of the project as indicated in Table
E3. Mitigation costs consist of two components, investment costs and costs of
operation covering the fields of noise pollution, air quality, marine management, solid
waste management and traffic control.

- Expenditure of tourists
Outflows of foreign exchange include:

- Foreign components in the cost of operation of the Airport (Annex E4) (based
on the financial feasibility study)
- Foreign components In the cost of operation of mitigation (Annex E5) (based

- Expenses on foreign exchange (15% of expenditure of tourists)
- Repatriation payment
- Repayment of loan and interest charges (Annex E6) (based on the financial

The relevant statements attached Illustrate the results of the direct and indirect
economic impacts for the new extension of SES Airport.
4. Interpretation of the Results
The conducted economic analysis of the new extension of SES Airport reveals that it is
highly viable from the society's point of view and is expected to have a positive economic
impact If all mitigation costs of environmental negative effect are considered. The derived
economic ratios indicate the following:
Economic Indicators
Item
ERR                                 49% (In Real Terms)
NPV                                 LE 6,529 Million
Absolute Efficiency Test (AET)      LE 13,522 Million
Relative Efficiency Test (RET)      LE 35 per Pound invested
Employment Effect                   5 Jobs per Million (2006), with an
annual increase of 19%
Foreign Exchange Effect             US $ 3,072 Million
Taxation Effect                     LE 3,982 Million
* The new extension of SES Airport is capable of creating a social surplus, with an
Economic Rate of Return (ERR) exceeding 49% (in real terms) and much greater
than the Social Opportunity Cost of Capital in Egypt (10% in real terms).
* The present value of the project as going concern (LE 6,949 Million) exceeds the
present value of the capital invested (LE 420 Million) resulting in a significant
positive net present value (LE 6,529 Million). This analysis indicates that the
proposed new extension of the Airport is economically viable.
* The new extension Is expected to create a positive national value added (LE
13,522 Million), which indicates that it will have a positive impact on the
economy.

Technical background
NOISE
Acoustic noise is usually defined as unwanted sound, an undesirable byproduct of
society's normal day-to-day activities.
THE DECIBEL:
The Decibel is the unit of sound measurement.
A-weighted Sound Level:
The frequency response of the measuring Sound Level Meter must follow
approximately a certain equal loudness curve (the ear's feeling of pressure variation
depends on the frequency of this variation).
The following reasons have led to the adoption of A-weighted sound level in many
national and international codes and standards:
1. It has been shown that it     ....            . . . ---   ........ ...............
correlates  well   with                    ..... ...   ..... ...........
subjective response and                       _      _     _

Equivalent     Continuous
Sound Level (LA.q):
LA,q is the A-weighted energy mean of the noise level averaged over the
measurement period. It can be considered as the continuous steady noise-level, which
would have the same total A-weighted acoustic energy as the real fluctuating noise
measured over the same period of time.
(      )
T     is the total measurement time
PACt) is the A-weighted instantaneous acoustic pressure

po    is the reference acoustic pressure (20 pPa)
Day - Night Sound Level, DNL
Noise levels occurring at night generally produce greater annoyance than the same
levels occurring during daytime. It is generally agreed that people perceive intrusive
noise at night as being 10 dBA louder than the same level of intrusive noise during
the day, at least in terms of its potential for causing community annoyance. This
perception is largely because background environmental sound levels at night in most
areas are also about 10 dBA lower than those during the day.
The DNL scale has been suggested by the US Environmental Protection Agency to
take into account the increased annoyance caused by noise at night. It is the average
sound level of 24-hours taking into calculation a 10 dB(A) penalty for sounds
occurring between 10 pm and 7 am.
The word 'Annoy" means:
1. to disturb or irritate especially by repeated acts
2. to harass especially by quick brief attacks
(Merriam Webster Online Dictionary)
Hence the word annoyance is the act of being annoyed, i.e. to be disturbed or
irritated by repeated acts. In our case this act is noise.
The first principle of the World Health Organization (WHO) Constitution is its definition
of health that is given as: "A state of complete physical, mental and social well-being
and not merely the absence of disease or infirmity." According this WHO definition of
health,  noise  impacts  such  as  population  annoyance, interference  with
communication, and-impaired task performance are health issues.
Noise can cause stress, high blood pressure, sleep loss, distraction and temporary or
even permanent hearing.
Annoyance due to noise is perceived different from person to person. Acousticians
have attempted to quantify this to enable objective assessment of noise nuisances
and implement acceptable noise limits. A Rating Level (LR) has been developed as an
attempt to put a numerical value on a noise to quantify its annoyance in the relation
to the general population. The rating level is defined in the ISO-1996 standard
(International Standards).
Propagation of Sound In Air:
In addition to the reduction in intensity with distance, there are many other factors
that can significantly affect the propagation of sound in a real medium like the
atmosphere:
1. Velocity and temperature gradients alter the direction of the wave.
2. Turbulence distorts it.
EIA for SES Terninal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Arnex H. - Noise



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                   u            -i      \
3. Viscosity causes absorption.
The last effect is far greater for high than for low frequencies, so the atmosphere
tends to act as a low pass filter, attenuating high frequencies, and thus distorting the
frequency spectrum of a noise source, as well as reducing its strength and changing
its propagation path.

Sound attenuation from an aircraft considered as a point source
Effects of Wind:
The atmosphere is in state of continuous motion over the earth's surface and is also a
real fluid with all the normal physical properties including viscosity. The velocity of the
molecules of air at ground level must be zero and the wind speed gradually increases
with height (boundary layer) until the speed of the main air mass is attained.
When a sound wave impinges on a layer of air which has a different speed, the wave's
direction changes. The overall effect as far as a stationary observer on the ground is
concerned, is to bend the downwind sound rays back towards the earth and bend the
upwind rays away from it, as shown in the following figure.

Sound refraction in a boundary layer
A region of noise reinforcement is therefore formed downwind of the source and a
sound shadow, a region of reduced intensity, occurs on its upwind side. Attenuations
in the shadow region may be as high as 30 dB but the increases that are due to
reinforcement downwind of the source are usually smaller.
Effect of Temperature Gradients:
The velocity of sound in air increases with temperature, and in norrnal atmosphere
the temperature itself decreases with height.
A rising sound ray, when entering a layer with a lower temperature, undergoes a
reduction in propagation velocity and is refracted away from the interface between
the two layers. The result is that, the rays are continuously bent away from the
ground surface, and a shadow region is formed at a distance from the source that
depends on the strength of the temperature gradient.  .

Sometimes, however, the temperature gradient near the ground is positive, i.e. the
temperature increases with height up to a point where it reverts to the normal lapse
rate (temperature inversion). The sound rays become refracted downwards towards
the ground as it progresses through the warmer layer of air, reinforces the sound field
at surface level around the source.
Effects of Humidity:
The absorption of sound in air varies with frequency, humidity, and temperature in an
extremely complicated fashion; the only general trend being that it is higher at high
frequencies, and shows a tendency to increase with temperature but to decrease at
higher relative humidity.
The appendix contains tables of sound attenuation coefficient in dB/100 m for 1/3
octave band analysis as a function of temperature and relative humidity.
The following graph shows the sound level in dBA for some famous sound sources.

1/3 Octave Analysis
Sound consists of many frequencies, each having its own sound power. The sum of
each frequency's sound power will give the total sound power.
The third octave analysis enables us to review the sound power of each frequency of a
certain sound source. The dominant frequency range gives us an indication on the
EIA for SES Termiinal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Annex H - Noise



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP X
nature of the sound source, e.g. the 1/3 octave analysis of an airplane (close range
measurement) should show high sound power levels of high frequencies above 1000
Hz, since the source of sound is the plane engine, most probably a gas turbine.
Sound analysis of a plane at a long distance should show high sound levels of low
frequencies since they are able to travel longer a distance.
Effect of Noise on Human Performance
The effects of noise are seldom catastrophic, and are often only transitory, but
adverse effects can be cumulative with prolonged or repeated exposure. Sleep
disruption, the masking of speech and television, and the inability to enjoy one's
property or leisure time impair the quality of life.
In addition, noise can interfere with the teaching and learning process, disrupt the
performance of certain tasks, and increase the incidence of antisocial behavior.
Annoyance due to noise is perceived different from person to person. Acousticians
have attempted to quantify this to enable objective assessment of noise nuisances
and implement acceptable noise limits. A Rating Level (LR) has been developed as an
attempt to put a numerical value on a noise to quantify its annoyance in the relation
to the general population. The rating level is defined in the ISO-1996 standard
(International Standards)
Instrumentation
All the instruments are manufactured by Bruel & Kjaer (B&K), the world's leading
company in noise measurement, located in Denmark.
Two main instruments were used in the measurements:
* Modular Precision Sound Analyzer Type 2260
* The Serial Number of the sound level meter is 2305245
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Annex H - Noise



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                              WAVL ,-flU\
,   J
Modular Precision Sound Analyzer Type 2260
The  instruments  were  calibrated  using  B&K  Sound   Level  Calibrator
Type 4231, which produces a reference sound of 94 dB. The calibration is performed
for the microphones and the instruments before and after each group of readings.
The microphones were mounted on Tripods Type UA0801 at a height of 1.2 meters
from the ground surface.
Standards:
The instruments conform to:
IEC651 (1979) and IEC804 (1985) Type 2;
ANSI S1.4 (1983) and draft S1.43 (1992) Type 2;
BS 5969 and BS 6698 Type 1.

1.       GENERAL

2.       SCOPE OF SUPPLY
The Bidder should supply, erect, install and startup the system for
hardware and software. The system consists of TEN [10] fixed Noise
Monitoring Terminal unit, TWO (2) of mobile Noise Monitoring units. The
NMT units should be equipped with suitable modem for public line and GSM
systems and TWO (2) NMT well be equipped with weather data logger. The
NMT units should be powered using solar cell system.
Fixed NMT units will be located according to map around Cairo International
airport.
A full description of each location will be investigated.
The central database computer will be at airport authority. The bidder
should supply three other terminals and three high-quality printers.
The Supplier should supply the equipment in a period of 3 month.
3.       PURPOSE
To monitor the noise level during Aircraft take off and landing for Cairo
International airport at a fixed station as well as mobile station around
greater Cairo

PART 2: LOCATION OF NOISE MONITORING STATIONS
2.1      GENERAL CONSIDERATIONS:
The choice of location for noise monitoring stations is the most important
criteria in obtaining accurate and useful noise data. Because the needs for
noise data may vary considerably, the scientific and engineering guidelines
for placing noise monitor stations may also differ considerably. The
selection of monitoring sites should be carefully considered early in the
development of a monitoring plan, once the objectives for the monitoring
system have been clearly identified.
Typically, noise monitoring information requirements may encompass
several different objectives. Because of initial installation and operating
costs, there is usually a desire to install the minimum number of stations
as are deemed required to meet the program objectives, although the
incremental cost of adding additional stations is often low compared with
the worth of the improved data obtained.
The selection of noise monitoring sites is usually a two-stage process. The
first stage involves the general location of the monitoring sites. This
general selection is based upon monitoring objectives, which might include:
a. to obtain accurate noise information in specific noise-sensitive
community areas.
b. To obtain accurate noise information for verifying noise contour
locations.
c. To obtain accurate information on the noise levels produced by different
types of aircraft at the particular location and operations for noise
regulatory (noise limit) purposes, noise budget analyses, etc.
d. To obtain noise information to monitor aircraft departure or landing
flight paths, and to determine runway and flight path utilization.
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Annex H - Noise



ENGINEERING CONSIJLTANTS GROUP                                Wu/2        ,4 &0
To meet noise monitoring system technical considerations, particularly the
need to obtain noise information from more than one station under
important departure or arrival paths for the screening of aircraft noise
signals from other community noises.
To monitor compliance with set daily sound exposure level requirements.
The second stage of the site selection process is the selection of specific
monitor sites within the general area. This is based upon practical
considerations such as:
Interference from other noise sources (road traffic, Industry, etc.) note: the
noise from trees caused by wind should not be overlooked as interference.
a. Ease of access to utilities (telephone and electrical power)
b. Terrain and building obstructions
c. Ease and costs of obtaining site access and approvals. (Location on
private property may require payments of rent or easements; location
on publicly owned land such as parkways may be less costly for public
agencies, but obtaining formal approvals may be difficult and/or time
consuming.)
d. Monitor station security considerations (vandalism and theft)
e. Extreme environmental conditions especially those, which are not
continuous
Basic planning for a monitoring system should include the development of
a reasonably complete set of sound level or time average level contours for
the airport, which cover the community areas of interest. The process of
collecting the operational and flight track information for the contours may
help to identify weak points in operational information (for example, lack of
runway utilization data or existence of major flight tracks beyond a few
miles distance from the airport) that may require further investigation
during the process of selecting noise monitor locations.
A set or sound level or time average level contours can be useful in
estimating relative differences in sound exposure level among candidate
monitor locations. After the monitoring system has been installed and
become operational, system noise data output can be valuablein improving
and refining the contours themselves. Variations in local topography,
particularly hilly terrain, can affect the propagation of sound from aircraft
to monitoring locations. Hills between an aircraft flight path and a
microphone can shield the microphone, as can intervene structures,
reducing measured sound levels. Microphones on high terrain can receive
higher levels because of decreased distance from the aircraft source.
EIA for SES Teminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Annex H - Noise



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                               'h=ki) ,            )1 s\
Placement of Monitors under Major Flight Tracks.
To obtain accurate information on runway utilization, i.e., to count the
number of arrivals and departures on each runway, it is generally is
desirable to place stations under or nearly under the primary dz c.r^o
arrival flight paths. The positions of these stations may be adjusted also to
provide accurate information on aircraft noise levels at appropriate
locations, for instance, at the nearest edge of a noise-sensitive land use
zone.
The placement of stations under major flight paths may aiso hp uqpRfiil
when the primary monitoring purpose is to determine contour locations or
to monitor noise in noise sensitive community areas. Monitoring at such
positions provides more accurate information about aircraft activity than
will monitoring far off the flight track centerline.
Noise information from monitor positions under major flight paths can be
valuable in separating the noise of aircraft from that of other sources at
different monitoring locations.
The time separation between noise events should be considered when
these are used to determine direction of flight and to separate aircraft and
non-aircraft noise. A time separation of at least three to five seconds
between noise events measured at different monitoring points is desirable.
Hence the spacing between stations, measured along the flight track,
40                   should be of the order of 500 meters or more assuming, for jet aircraft,
operating speeds in the range of 120 to 160 knots.
Note: It is sometimes useful to place noise monitors near the ends of
active runways where they will receive 'strong aircraft signals and be
subject to fewer non-aircraft noise events. This may not always prove
desirable, however, because there can be many noise sources within the
airport boundaries which produce quite high local noise levels. Such
sources include taxiing aircraft, helicopter operations, maintenance vehicles,
engine runups, etc. Thus, for positions very close to the runway,
investigation is needed to preclude contamination of aircraft operational
noise.
Reference Position
It is recommended that at least one monitoring position shall be as close to
a point lkm from the runway threshold as is possible allowing for any
obstructions.
Note: one important advantage of a 'standardised' lkm monitoring point is
that it allows comparison of 'in service' noise between different operators
and equipment, also comparison of noise at several airports.
Monitors to Determine Contour Boundaries
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Annex H -Noise



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                                   -4    b)
For monitoring to enable correlation with noise contour locations, stations
should be placed at or near the expected contour locations in or near noise-
sensitive areas. Since contours may extend quite far to the side of flight
tracks, the location of such stations should be coordinated with the location
of monitors near the flight tracks, so that noise information froiri i'ilt idiUer
stations can be used to help separate aircraft from non-aircraft events at
the other monitors.
In selecting monitoring stations in relation to contour determination, exact
placement on the expected contour line may not be practical. Monitoring
stations should preferably be placed outboard of the contours, provided this
does not result in undue reduction of aircraft levels or risk of contamination
from non-aircraft noise sources. This provides a conservative approach in
estimating the noise contour location since to do so one must interpolate
inward towards the airport runways or major flight tracks rather than
outward.
Note: unless a sufficient number of monitoring points are employed, it may
be very difficult if not impossible to correlate measured noise with known
or predicted noise contours.
Monitors for Specific Noise-Sensitive Areas
There may be special problems in selecting monitor sites in identified
noise-sensitive community areas. When these areas are located under or
near major flight paths close to the airport, placement of monitors presents
no special problems. However, when a noise-sensitive area is remote from
the airport and flight paths, aircraft noise levels may be relatively low in
comparison to levels from other community noise sources. While the total
sound exposure levels may be measured easily, it may be very difficult to
separate the desired category of aircraft noise from other noise
contributions. For such locations, extensive preliminary monitoring,
together with on-site field observations, may be needed to identify the
actual sources of noise. Special consideration should be given to means for
correlating aircraft noise signals at such positions with the noise signals at
close-in monitoring stations in order to achieve adequate discrimination of
aircraft signals of interest from other noise.
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Annex H - Noise

The World Health Organization Limits
The World Health Organization (WHO, 1999) recommends (Table5) a 16-hour daytime
LEQ of 55 dB and, approximately, 45 dB nighttime LEQ to prevent "serious
annoyance." These numbers are equivalent to a DNL of 55 dB. WHO further
recommends that, during the night, the maximum level (fast) of any single event not
exceed 60 dB. To prevent annoyance, WHO recommends levels that are 5 decibels
lower-a daytime LEQ of 50 dB and a nighttime LEQ of 40 dB. These numbers are
equivalent to a DNL of 50 dB.
Table 5: WHO DNL Criteria for Noise Annoyance in Residential Areas (The
LAmaxLevel is for Protecting from Sleep Disruption.)
Impact       Daytime   Nighttime  Approximate  Nighttime
charactedzation   LEQ       LEQ        DNL       LaMax
Serious Annoyance  55        45          55
Moderate Annoyance  50        40         50         60

The World Bank Group
The World Bank Group (WBG, 1998) has developed a strong program in nollution
management so as to insure that their projects in developing countries are
environmentally sound. Noise is one of the pollutants covered by their policy. They set
the following noise limits for general industrial projects including foundries, iron and
steel manufacturing, and thermal power plants
Table 6: World Bank Noise limits for industrial projects to which money is lent
Receptor   Time Period  Time Period LEQ  Equivalent DNL
Residential,  Daytime         55              55
institutional,  Nigtie4
eduafional    ighttme         45
Industrial,  Daytime         70
commercial   Nighttime        70
The International Organization for Economic Co-operation and Development
The International Organization for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD)
has similar concerns to those expressed by the policy of the World Bank Group. OECD
has set "Pollution Prevention and Control Environmental Criteria for Sustainable
Transport" (OECD, 1996). They state: "Noise finds a place among these criteria on
account of the high level of concem about noise from motorized transport and the
possible adverse impacts of noise on human health and quality of life." OECD goes on
to support the levels recommended by WHO. Further, they suggest the following
environmentally sustainable transport noise levels based on the (noise) receiving
community clearly, like the WBG, OECD recommends a DNL of 55 dB, and, in rural
areas, it lowers its recommendation to DNL 50 dB.
Table 7: OECD suggested transport noise levels for the land area indicated
Land Area Time Period Time Period LEQ Equivalent DNL
Urbran    3Daytime         55             55
Nighttime        45
Rural     Daytime          50             50
Nighttime        40

Model Input, Output and Assumptions
Model Input includes:
1. Airport Information
Latitude and longitude
Level with respect to sea level
Humidity and temperature
2. Runway Information
Runway length and width
Runway ends latitude and longitude
Runway elevation
3. Track Information
Number of track
Types of track, departure or arrival
4. Airplane Information
Types of Airplanes
Landing and take off profile
5. Flight Operations
Sum of each type of airplane arriving
Sum of each type of airplane departing
Track usage
Local time of the movements
Model Output includes the following:
Case Echo Report
Noise Contours
Noise level vs. area
Model AssumDtions
The model used the current air traffic operations in SES Airport as follows:
Arrival
Normally, most of the arrival traffic operations use the Runway (04L - 22R). This
runway is equipped with Navigation Aids. Only when the prevailing wind direction
changes, aircrafts use the other Runway (22R- 04L) i.e. from the opposite direction.
Generally, the arrival track is 04L - 23R.
Departure
Most of the departure traffic operations (local or international) use the Runway (04L -
22R).
EIA for SES Terminal Airport Extension Project (Rev. 0)
Annex H - Noise



ENGINEERING CONSULTANTS GROUP                              CA)D4J) ,4          '
The air traffic movements for the last two months were reviewed. This includes for
each day type of airplane, owner, time of departure, time of arrival and airplane
destination.
The data have been processed to the INM 6.0c. This is followed by carrying out a
count with the following layout:
6. Type of airplane
7. Track used
8. Count of day flights
9. Count of evening flights
10. Count of night flights
It was also assumed in the Model, that the planes used their maximum carrying
capacity, maximum take off and maximum landing power.
